Task instruction sent to agent 
# Architecture Document: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** envoyproxy/envoy
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Task

Produce an architecture document for Envoy's **HTTP Connection Manager** (HCM) subsystem. The document must explain how the major components interact to process an HTTP request from arrival on a downstream connection through to upstream dispatch. Do not simply list APIs — explain the **design**, **data flow**, and **extension points**.

## Scope

Your document must cover these four components and how they work together:

### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl
The central network filter that owns the connection lifecycle. Explain:
- How it implements `Network::ReadFilter` to receive raw bytes
- How it creates and manages `ActiveStream` objects for each HTTP request
- Its role in codec creation (lazy codec instantiation for H1/H2 vs. H3)
- Connection-level concerns: drain decisions, overload management, watermark-based flow control

### 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain
The per-stream filter chain execution engine. Explain:
- The decoder filter chain (request path) and encoder filter chain (response path)
- How `FilterChainFactory` creates filters for each stream
- Filter iteration: how `decodeHeaders`/`decodeData`/`decodeTrailers` propagate through decoder filters
- How filters can stop iteration, modify headers, or send local replies
- The distinction between `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, and `StreamFilter` (dual)

### 3. Router Filter
The terminal decoder filter that forwards requests upstream. Explain:
- Route selection: how the router uses `RouteConfiguration` to pick a cluster
- How it obtains an HTTP connection pool from `ClusterManager`
- Upstream request lifecycle: `UpstreamRequest` creation, retry logic, timeout handling
- Shadow routing and hedged request support (if applicable)

### 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity
The upstream connection pool and cluster management layer. Explain:
- How `ClusterManagerImpl` provides connection pools per cluster
- Load balancing: how the router obtains a host from the cluster's load balancer
- Connection pool mechanics: the relationship between logical connection pools and physical connections
- How health checking and outlier detection feed back into the load balancer

## Document Requirements

1. **Component Responsibilities** — what each component owns
2. **Data Flow** — the path of an HTTP request from downstream bytes to upstream dispatch, and the response path back
3. **Extension Points** — where users extend Envoy (HTTP filters, cluster extensions, load balancers, access loggers)
4. **Error Handling** — how errors at each stage (codec errors, filter errors, upstream failures) are handled
5. **relevant source files** — reference the actual source files in the envoyproxy/envoy repository

## Anti-Requirements

- Do NOT generate a simple API listing or header-file dump
- Do NOT fabricate class names or file paths that don't exist in the repository
- Do NOT cover Envoy components outside the HCM request path (e.g., xDS config delivery, listener management)

   354→
   355→const FilterUtility::StrictHeaderChecker::HeaderCheckResult
   356→FilterUtility::StrictHeaderChecker::checkHeader(Http::RequestHeaderMap& headers,
   357→                                                const Http::LowerCaseString& target_header) {
   358→  if (target_header == Http::Headers::get().EnvoyUpstreamRequestTimeoutMs) {
   359→    return isInteger(headers.EnvoyUpstreamRequestTimeoutMs());
   360→  } else if (target_header == Http::Headers::get().EnvoyUpstreamRequestPerTryTimeoutMs) {
   361→    return isInteger(headers.EnvoyUpstreamRequestPerTryTimeoutMs());
   362→  } else if (target_header == Http::Headers::get().EnvoyMaxRetries) {
   363→    return isInteger(headers.EnvoyMaxRetries());
   364→  } else if (target_header == Http::Headers::get().EnvoyRetryOn) {
   365→    return hasValidRetryFields(headers.EnvoyRetryOn(), &Router::RetryStateImpl::parseRetryOn);
   366→  } else if (target_header == Http::Headers::get().EnvoyRetryGrpcOn) {
   367→    return hasValidRetryFields(headers.EnvoyRetryGrpcOn(),
   368→                               &Router::RetryStateImpl::parseRetryGrpcOn);
   369→  }
   370→  // Should only validate headers for which we have implemented a validator.
   371→  PANIC("unexpectedly reached");
   372→}

   560→Network::FilterStatus ConnectionManagerImpl::onNewConnection() {

   570→  // onData() interface because QUICHE already handles de-multiplexing.
   571→  return Network::FilterStatus::StopIteration;

67-assistanttext-
The architecture document has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

---

## Document Summary

The document explains how the four HCM components interact to process an HTTP request from downstream bytes to upstream dispatch and back, organized as follows:

### 1. `ConnectionManagerImpl`
- How it implements `Network::ReadFilter` and receives raw bytes via `onData()`
- **Lazy codec creation**: H1/H2 codecs are instantiated on the first `onData()` call by inspecting the initial bytes; H3 (QUIC) creates the codec eagerly in `onNewConnection()` and bypasses `onData()` entirely
- `newStream()` allocates `ActiveStream` objects and prepends them to a linked list
- Connection-level drain decisions, overload shedding via two `LoadShedPoint` handles, watermark-based flow control delegated into the codec, and per-connection idle/duration timers

### 2. `FilterManager` and the HTTP Filter Chain
- `StreamDecoderFilters` iterates forward (A→B→C); `StreamEncoderFilters` iterates in **reverse** (C→B→A) for symmetric request/response wrapping
- `FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` populates both vectors once per stream before the first headers arrive
- `decodeHeaders()` / `decodeData()` / `decodeTrailers()` iteration with `Continue`, `StopIteration`, and `StopAllIteration` semantics; how `continueDecoding()` resumes a paused chain
- `sendLocalReply()` aborts the decoder chain and synthesizes a response through the encoder chain

### 3. Router Filter
- Route selection via `RouteConfiguration` match against `:authority`, path, and headers
- Thread-local, lock-free cluster lookup via `getThreadLocalCluster()`
- `UpstreamRequest` lifecycle: host selection, `GenericConnPool` creation, the upstream `FilterManager` / `UpstreamCodecFilter` sub-c
... (truncated)

This should reduce the heap allocation and\n// memory fragmentation.\n\n// HTTP decoder filters. If filters are configured in the following order (assume all three\n// filters are both decoder/encoder filters):\n//   http_filters:\n//     - A\n//     - B\n//     - C\n// The decoder filter chain will iterate through filters A, B, C.\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n  using Element = ActiveStreamDecoderFilter;\n  using Iterator = std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr>::iterator;\n\n  Iterator begin() { return entries_.begin(); }\n  Iterator end() { return entries_.end(); }\n\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n};\n\n// HTTP encoder filters.     StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamConnectionTermination))) {\n      stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ConnectError);\n    } else {\n      const bool StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamProtocolError) &&\n          !Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\n              \"envoy.reloadable_features.reset_ignore_upstream_reason\")) {\n {
  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager: Architecture Document\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP traffic. It is implemented as a `Network::ReadFilter` \u2014 a plugin in Envoy's L4 filter chain \u2014 that takes ownership of a downstream TCP (or QUIC) connection and converts the raw byte stream into a sequence of HTTP request/response lifecycle events. Four primary components collaborate to move a request from arrival on the wire to dispatch upstream and back:\n\n1. **`ConnectionManagerImpl`** \u2014 owns the connection and its codec; creates `ActiveStream` objects per request.\n2. **`FilterManager` / `DownstreamFilterManager`** \u2014 owns the per-stream HTTP filter chain and drives it forward.\n3. **Router `Filter`** \u2014 the terminal decoder filter; selects a cluster, obtains a connection pool, and forwards the request.\n4. **`ClusterManagerImpl`** \u2014 manages cluster topology, load balancing, and connection pools.\n\nThe source code lives primarily under:\n\n| Component | Source files |\n|---|---|\n| ConnectionManagerImpl | `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.{h,cc}` |\n| FilterManager | `source/common/http/filter_manager.{h,cc}` |\n| Router Filter | `source/common/router/router.{h,cc}`, `source/common/router/upstream_request.{h,cc}` |\n| ClusterManager | `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.{h,cc}` |\n| HTTP/1 codec | `source/common/http/http1/` |\n| HTTP/2 codec | `source/common/http/http2/` |\n| Connection pools | `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.{h,cc}`, `source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.*`, `source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.*`, `source/common/http/conn_pool_grid.*` |\n| Outlier detection | `source/common/upstream/outlier_detection_impl.{h,cc}` |\n| Health checking | `source/common/upstream/health_checker_impl.{h,cc}` |\n\n---\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl` (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h`) is the network-layer entry point for HTTP traffic. It implements three interfaces simultaneously:\n\n- **`Network::ReadFilter`** \u2014 receives raw bytes arriving on the downstream TCP connection.\n- **`Http::ServerConnectionCallbacks`** \u2014 receives per-stream notifications from the HTTP codec (new stream, GoAway).\n- **`Network::ConnectionCallbacks`** \u2014 receives connection-level events (close, watermark changes).\n\nIt is instantiated once per downstream connection by the HCM extension factory (`source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc`) and wired into Envoy's L4 filter chain at connection acceptance time.\n\n### Codec Creation (Lazy Instantiation)\n\nFor HTTP/1.x and HTTP/2, `ConnectionManagerImpl` does not create a codec until the first `onData()` call arrives:\n\n```\n// source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc, onData()\nif (!codec_) {\n    createCodec(data);\n}\nconst Status status = codec_->dispatch(data);\n```\n\n`createCodec()` delegates to `ConnectionManagerConfig::createCodec()`, which inspects the first bytes of `data` to distinguish HTTP/1 from HTTP/2 (the H2 client preface `PRI * HTTP/2.0\\r\\n\\r\\nSM\\r\\n\\r\\n`). The resulting `ServerConnection` (H1 or H2 implementation) is stored in `codec_`.\n\nFor HTTP/3 (QUIC), the protocol is known at connection time, so the codec is created eagerly in `onNewConnection()` before any `onData()` arrives:\n\n```\n// source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc, onNewConnection()\ncreateCodec(dummy);\nASSERT(codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http3);\nreturn Network::FilterStatus::StopIteration; // QUIC bypasses onData entirely\n```\n\nThis means H3 connections stop L4 filter iteration immediately; QUICHE handles stream demultiplexing internally and delivers decoded events directly to the codec callbacks.\n\n### ActiveStream Creation\n\nWhen the codec parses a complete set of request headers from the wire, it calls back `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()`. This function:\n\n1. Allocates a `Buffer::BufferMemoryAccount` for watermark tracking, wired to the downstream `ResponseEncoder`.\n2. Constructs an `ActiveStream` object, giving it a back-reference to the `ConnectionManagerImpl` and a `DownstreamFilterManager`.\n3. Prepends the new stream to the `streams_` linked list and returns it as the `RequestDecoder` for the codec to use for subsequent `decodeHeaders` / `decodeData` / `decodeTrailers` calls.\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\nauto new_stream = std::make_unique<ActiveStream>(\n    *this, response_encoder.getStream().bufferLimit(), std::move(downstream_stream_account));\nLinkedList::moveIntoList(std::move(new_stream), streams_);\nreturn **streams_.begin();\n```\n\n`ActiveStream` is a heavyweight struct that aggregates the `DownstreamFilterManager`, cached route, request/response header maps, timers, and tracing span for a single HTTP exchange. It implements `RequestDecoder` so the codec can push bytes into it, and `FilterManagerCallbacks` so the filter chain can push encoded responses back toward the codec.\n\n### Connection-Level Concerns\n\n**Drain decisions.** `ConnectionManagerImpl` holds a reference to `Network::DrainDecision`. On each new stream, it checks `maxRequestsPerConnection`; when that limit is reached on H2/H3, it calls `startDrainSequence()` which sends a GOAWAY frame and transitions to `DrainState::Draining`. When the stream count reaches zero, `checkForDeferredClose()` closes the TCP connection.\n\n**Overload management.** Two `Server::LoadShedPoint` handles are acquired at construction from `OverloadManager`:\n- `HcmDecodeHeaders` \u2014 checked at `decodeHeaders` time; sheds load by sending 503 and stopping iteration.\n- `HcmCodecCreation` \u2014 checked in `onData()` before codec instantiation; closes the connection before any work is done.\n\nAdditionally, two `OverloadActionState` references \u2014 `overload_stop_accepting_requests_ref_` and `overload_disable_keepalive_ref_` \u2014 are cached at construction and checked in the hot path without requiring a map lookup.\n\n**Watermark-based flow control.** The `ConnectionManagerImpl` implements `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` and `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`, which delegate directly into the codec:\n\n```cpp\nvoid onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark() override {\n    codec_->onUnderlyingConnectionAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark();\n}\n```\n\nThe H2 codec propagates these signals to per-stream flow control windows; the H1 codec pauses reads on the connection. Individual `ActiveStream` objects also track watermark state and propagate it to the decoder filter chain via `FilterManager::onDecoderFilterAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()`.\n\n**Request deferral across I/O cycles.** The runtime key `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` limits how many requests can be fully processed in a single read event. Additional requests are deferred to a schedulable callback (`deferred_request_processing_callback_`). This prevents a single connection from monopolizing the event loop under H2 or H3 multiplexing.\n\n**Timers per connection.** `initializeReadFilterCallbacks()` arms:\n- `connection_idle_timer_` \u2014 fires `onIdleTimeout()` if no streams are active for the configured duration.\n- `connection_duration_timer_` \u2014 fires `onConnectionDurationTimeout()` after the maximum connection age.\n\nThese are _connection-level_ timers that coexist with the _per-stream_ timers managed inside `ActiveStream`.\n\n### Error Handling\n\nCodec errors (protocol violations, buffer flood attacks, inbound frames with empty payloads, overload errors) are caught at the `codec_->dispatch(data)` call site. `handleCodecError()` and `handleCodecOverloadError()` record the appropriate response flag, then call `doConnectionClose()` with `FlushWriteAndDelay`, which:\n1. Resets all active streams with `StreamResetReason::ConnectionTermination`.\n2. Calls `connection().close()` on the underlying network connection.\n\n---\n\n## 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain\n\n### Class Hierarchy\n\n`FilterManager` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.h`) is the abstract base; `DownstreamFilterManager` is the concrete subclass used for downstream (client-to-proxy) streams. A separate `UpstreamFilterManager` is used for the upstream side inside `UpstreamRequest`. `FilterManager` owns two parallel vectors:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/filter_manager.h\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n    std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n    // Iterates forward: A -> B -> C\n};\n\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n    std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n    // Iterates in reverse: C -> B -> A\n};\n```\n\nEach entry wraps a user-provided filter handle (`StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, or `StreamFilter` for dual-purpose) and tracks per-filter iteration state.\n\n### Filter Chain Construction\n\n`FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` is called once per stream during `ActiveStream` initialization, before the first `decodeHeaders` call. The HCM configuration object (`source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc`) implements `FilterChainFactory`. It iterates over the ordered list of `HttpFilterFactory` functions configured via `http_filters`, calling:\n\n```cpp\ncallbacks.addStreamDecoderFilter(filter);\ncallbacks.addStreamEncoderFilter(filter);\n// or, for dual-purpose filters:\ncallbacks.addStreamFilter(filter);\n```\n\nThese append `ActiveStreamDecoderFilter` or `ActiveStreamEncoderFilter` wrappers to the respective vectors. The router filter (the terminal filter) is always last in the decoder chain; the `UpstreamCodecFilter` is always last in the upstream filter chain.\n\n### Decoder Filter Iteration (Request Path)\n\nWhen `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` is called by the codec, it validates the header map (if UHV is enabled) and then calls `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()`. This function iterates `decoder_filters_` from beginning to end, calling each filter's `decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` method:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/filter_manager.cc\nfor (; entry != decoder_filters_.end(); entry++) {\n    FilterHeadersStatus status = (*entry)->handle_->decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream);\n    const auto continue_iteration =\n        (*entry)->commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback(status, end_stream);\n    if (!continue_iteration && std::next(entry) != decoder_filters_.end()) {\n        maybeContinueDecoding(continue_data_entry);\n        return; // pause here\n    }\n}\n```\n\nA filter controls iteration by its return value:\n\n| Return value | Effect |\n|---|---|\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::Continue` | Proceed to the next filter immediately. |\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::StopIteration` | Pause iteration; filter must later call `continueDecoding()`. |\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::StopAllIterationAndBuffer` | Pause and buffer all subsequent data until resumed. |\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::StopAllIterationAndWatermark` | Pause and apply watermark-based back pressure. |\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::ContinueAndDontEndStream` | Continue but strip the end-stream flag (allows injecting a body). |\n\n`decodeData()` and `decodeTrailers()` follow the same pattern. Each call records a `latest_data_decoding_filter_` pointer so that subsequent data injected by a filter is only forwarded to filters _after_ the injecting filter, preventing double-processing.\n\n### Resuming Iteration\n\n`ActiveStreamDecoderFilter::continueDecoding()` calls `commonContinue()` on the base class. This:\n1. Sets `iteration_state_` back to `Continue`.\n2. If the filter had stopped with `StopAll`, sets `iterate_from_current_filter_ = true` so iteration restarts from the paused filter rather than the next one.\n3. Resumes `do1xxHeaders()`, `doHeaders()`, `doData()`, and `doTrailers()` in order.\n\n### Encoder Filter Iteration (Response Path)\n\nWhen the router filter receives a response from upstream, it calls back into the `FilterManager` via `FilterManagerCallbacks::encodeHeaders()`. The `FilterManager` iterates `encoder_filters_` in **reverse** order (last-configured to first-configured), ensuring symmetric wrapping: a filter that transforms the request also wraps the response.\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/filter_manager.h\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n    using Iterator = std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr>::reverse_iterator;\n    Iterator begin() { return entries_.rbegin(); }\n    Iterator end()   { return entries_.rend(); }\n};\n```\n\n### Local Replies\n\nAny filter may call `sendLocalReply(code, body, modify_headers, grpc_status, details)` to terminate the request without forwarding it upstream. This:\n1. Sets a `LocalReplyOwnerObject` in filter state identifying the originating filter.\n2. Delegates to `FilterManager::sendLocalReply()`, which synthesizes a response header map and runs it through the encoder filter chain.\n3. Sets `decoder_filter_chain_aborted_ = true`, causing all subsequent decoder filter calls to short-circuit.\n\n### Filter Type Taxonomy\n\n| Interface | Direction | When used |\n|---|---|---|\n| `StreamDecoderFilter` | Request only | Auth filters, body inspection, header manipulation |\n| `StreamEncoderFilter` | Response only | Response compression, header stripping |\n| `StreamFilter` | Both | External processing (ext_proc), WASM, Lua filters |\n\nAll three share `StreamFilterBase::onDestroy()` for cleanup when the stream ends.\n\n### Access Logging\n\n`FilterManager` accumulates access log handlers from two sources: the HCM-level `accessLogs()` list from `ConnectionManagerConfig`, and per-filter handlers added via `FilterManagerCallbacks::accessLogHandlers()`. These are merged in `ActiveStream::accessLogHandlers()` and fired on stream completion.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Router Filter\n\n### Role in the Pipeline\n\nThe router filter (`source/common/router/router.h`, class `Filter`) is always the last filter in the decoder chain. It implements `Http::StreamDecoderFilter` and `Upstream::LoadBalancerContextBase`. Unlike most filters that transform traffic and pass it along, the router filter consumes the request and originates a new one upstream via `UpstreamRequest`.\n\n### Route Selection\n\nIn `Filter::decodeHeaders()`, after validation of strict check headers, route selection proceeds:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/router/router.cc\nroute_ = callbacks_->route();\n```\n\n`callbacks_->route()` calls into `ActiveStream::route()`, which consults the snapped `RouteConfiguration` (an `ActiveStream`-local snapshot of the RDS configuration taken when the stream begins). The route configuration (`source/common/router/config_impl.cc`) evaluates each `VirtualHost` and its `Route` entries in configuration order, matching on `:authority`, path prefix/regex/exact, headers, and query parameters. The first match wins.\n\nIf no route matches, the router sends a 404 via `sendLocalReply()` and returns `StopIteration`.\n\nIf the matched route has a `direct_response`, the router synthesizes the configured response locally and never contacts upstream.\n\nIf the matched route has a `route_entry`, the router extracts `route_entry_->clusterName()` and looks up the cluster:\n\n```cpp\nUpstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster =\n    config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName());\n```\n\nThis lookup is thread-local and lock-free (see \u00a74). If the cluster does not exist, a 503 with `NoClusterFound` response flag is returned.\n\n### Host Selection and Connection Pool Acquisition\n\nAfter cluster lookup, the router calls `cluster->chooseHost(this)` where `this` implements `LoadBalancerContext`. This interface provides:\n- `computeHashKey()` \u2014 for consistent-hash load balancers, derived from header-based hash policy configured on the route or cluster.\n- `metadataMatchCriteria()` \u2014 for metadata-based subset routing.\n- `downstreamConnection()` \u2014 allows the LB to read downstream SSL/connection attributes.\n\nHost selection may be synchronous (common case) or asynchronous (e.g., when waiting for an on-demand cluster). In the synchronous path, `continueDecodeHeaders()` is called immediately. In the asynchronous path, the filter returns `StopAllIterationAndWatermark` and stores a callback to resume when the host is ready.\n\nOnce a host is selected, `createConnPool()` obtains a `GenericConnPool` from the cluster's factory:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/router/router.cc\nstd::unique_ptr<GenericConnPool> generic_conn_pool = createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host);\n```\n\nThe `GenericConnPool` wraps an HTTP or TCP connection pool selected based on the route's `upstream_protocol` (HTTP, TCP for CONNECT tunneling, or UDP for CONNECT-UDP).\n\n### UpstreamRequest Lifecycle\n\n`UpstreamRequest` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.h`) encapsulates a single attempt to forward the request to a specific upstream host. The router may hold multiple `UpstreamRequest` objects simultaneously (one primary + hedged retries).\n\n```cpp\nUpstreamRequestPtr upstream_request = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(\n    *this, std::move(generic_conn_pool), can_send_early_data,\n    can_use_http3, enable_half_close);\nLinkedList::moveIntoList(std::move(upstream_request), upstream_requests_);\nupstream_requests_.front()->acceptHeadersFromRouter(end_stream);\n```\n\nInternally, `UpstreamRequest` owns an `UpstreamFilterManager` (a second, upstream-side filter chain). Headers and body flow through this chain until they reach the terminal `UpstreamCodecFilter`, which writes them to the upstream HTTP codec. If the upstream connection is not yet ready, `UpstreamCodecFilter` returns `StopAllIteration`, causing the `UpstreamFilterManager` to buffer data and apply watermarks back toward the router.\n\nWhen the upstream connection pool signals success via `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks::onPoolReady()`, the `UpstreamCodecFilter` flushes buffered data and begins streaming.\n\nResponse data arriving from upstream travels the reverse path: the upstream codec delivers frames to `UpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders()` / `decodeData()` / `decodeTrailers()`, which feed back through the `UpstreamFilterManager` and then call `RouterFilterInterface` callbacks on the `Filter`, which in turn calls `FilterManagerCallbacks::encodeHeaders()` to begin the downstream encoder filter chain.\n\n### Retry Logic\n\n`retry_state_` is created in `continueDecodeHeaders()` from the route's `RetryPolicy`:\n\n```cpp\nretry_state_ = createRetryState(*getEffectiveRetryPolicy(), headers, *cluster_,\n                                 request_vcluster_, route_stats_context_,\n                                 config_->factory_context_, callbacks_->dispatcher(),\n                                 route_entry_->priority());\n```\n\n`RetryStateImpl` (`source/common/router/retry_state_impl.cc`) tracks the number of attempts, retry-on conditions (5xx, reset, connect-failure, retriable status codes), and the current backoff interval. When an `UpstreamRequest` fails (connection error, 5xx response, per-try timeout), the router calls `retry_state_->shouldRetry()`. If retrying, a new `UpstreamRequest` is constructed and prepended to `upstream_requests_`, and the failed one is reset and removed.\n\n### Timeout Handling\n\n`FilterUtility::finalTimeout()` computes two timeouts:\n\n- **Global timeout** \u2014 enforced by a timer on `ActiveStream` (`max_stream_duration_timer_`). When it fires, the router sends a 504 locally.\n- **Per-try timeout** \u2014 set up via `UpstreamRequest::setupPerTryTimeout()`. When it fires, the current attempt is reset and retried (if `hedge_on_per_try_timeout` is configured, a new attempt is started _before_ the old one is cancelled, enabling hedging).\n\n### Shadow Routing\n\nIn `continueDecodeHeaders()`, after the primary `UpstreamRequest` is created, the router evaluates shadow policies from the route or cluster configuration. For each active shadow:\n\n```cpp\nHttp::AsyncClient::OngoingRequest* shadow_stream =\n    config_->shadowWriter().streamingShadow(cluster_name, shadow_headers, options);\n```\n\n`ShadowWriterImpl` (`source/common/router/shadow_writer_impl.cc`) sends the mirrored request via the HTTP async client. Shadow responses are discarded. Shadow streams are tracked in `shadow_streams_` and cancelled on stream destruction.\n\n### Error Handling\n\n| Failure | Router action |\n|---|---|\n| No route | `sendLocalReply(404, RouteNotFound)` |\n| Cluster not found | `sendLocalReply(503, ClusterNotFound)` |\n| No healthy upstream | `sendLocalReply(503, NoHealthyUpstream)` |\n| Maintenance mode | `sendLocalReply(503, MaintenanceMode)` |\n| Connection pool failure | Reset `UpstreamRequest`; check `retry_state_` |\n| Upstream 5xx / reset | Consult `retry_state_`; retry or propagate 5xx downstream |\n| Global timeout | `sendLocalReply(504, ResponseTimeout)` |\n| Per-try timeout (hedging off) | Reset attempt; retry if budget allows |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n### ClusterManagerImpl Architecture\n\n`ClusterManagerImpl` (`source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h`) is a singleton that maintains all cluster state in a thread-safe manner. Because Envoy uses a single-threaded event loop per worker thread, the cluster manager uses a thread-local storage pattern:\n\n- **Main thread** holds authoritative `ClusterData` objects (the `active_clusters_` and `warming_clusters_` maps).\n- **Each worker thread** holds a `ThreadLocalClusterManagerImpl` with its own `thread_local_clusters_` map, each containing per-host connection pools.\n\nCluster updates (from xDS/CDS) are applied on the main thread and then posted to all worker threads via `tls_.runOnAllThreads()`. This means each worker thread sees a consistent snapshot of cluster state without locks.\n\nThe `getThreadLocalCluster(name)` method (called by the router on the hot path) performs a simple hash map lookup against `thread_local_clusters_` \u2014 no locking, no cross-thread communication.\n\n### Load Balancing\n\nEach `ThreadLocalClusterManagerImpl::ClusterEntry` owns a `LoadBalancer` instance specific to that worker thread. When the router calls `cluster->chooseHost(context)`, it delegates to `lb_->chooseHost(context)`. Envoy ships several built-in load balancer implementations:\n\n- **Round robin** (`source/common/upstream/round_robin_lb.cc`) \u2014 cycles through the healthy host set.\n- **Least request** (`source/common/upstream/least_request_lb.cc`) \u2014 picks the host with fewest active requests using O(2) power-of-two-choices sampling.\n- **Random** (`source/common/upstream/random_lb.cc`) \u2014 uniform random selection.\n- **Ring hash / Maglev** (`source/common/upstream/ring_hash_lb.cc`, `maglev_lb.cc`) \u2014 consistent hashing; uses `LoadBalancerContext::computeHashKey()`.\n- **Subset LB** (`source/common/upstream/subset_lb.cc`) \u2014 wraps another LB; selects hosts matching `MetadataMatchCriteria`.\n\nAll built-in LBs operate on the **priority set** \u2014 an ordered collection of `HostSet` objects, one per priority level. Hosts that fail health checks or outlier detection are removed from the healthy set and are not selected.\n\n### Connection Pool Mechanics\n\n`ClusterEntry::httpConnPool()` (in `cluster_manager_impl.cc`) returns an `HttpPoolData` wrapping an `Http::ConnectionPool::Instance`:\n\n```cpp\nabsl::optional<HttpPoolData>\nClusterEntry::httpConnPool(HostConstSharedPtr host, ResourcePriority priority,\n                           absl::optional<Http::Protocol> protocol,\n                           LoadBalancerContext* context) {\n    auto pool = httpConnPoolImpl(host, priority, protocol, context);\n    ...\n    HttpPoolData data([this, priority, protocol, context]() {\n        maybePreconnect(...); // preconnect on each new stream\n    }, pool);\n    return data;\n}\n```\n\nEach pool is keyed by `(host, priority, protocol)`. Pools are created lazily on first use and are stored in `PriorityConnPoolMap<Http::ConnectionPool::Instance>`.\n\nThe concrete pool classes are:\n- `Http1ConnPoolImpl` (`source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.cc`) \u2014 one request per TCP connection; connections are not reused until the response is complete.\n- `Http2ConnPoolImpl` (`source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.cc`) \u2014 multiplexes many streams over one TCP connection; governed by `max_concurrent_streams`.\n- `ConnPoolGrid` (`source/common/http/conn_pool_grid.cc`) \u2014 tries HTTP/3 first (if QUIC is available), with automatic fallback to HTTP/2 or HTTP/1. Uses `HttpServerPropertiesCache` to remember per-origin protocol capabilities.\n\nThe shared base `HttpConnPoolImplBase` (`source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h`) implements stream queuing via `HttpPendingStream` objects. When `newStream()` is called:\n1. If a ready connection exists with capacity, the stream is attached immediately via `onPoolReady()`.\n2. Otherwise, a `HttpPendingStream` is enqueued. When a connection becomes available (either an existing one frees capacity, or a new one finishes the TLS handshake), the pending stream is dequeued and attached.\n\n**Preconnect.** After each new stream is established, `maybePreconnect()` is called speculatively to open an additional connection if the predicted load warrants it. The decision is based on `peekahead_ratio` and current `pending_streams_ / connecting_and_connected_stream_capacity_` ratios, mirroring the logic in `ConnPoolImplBase::shouldConnect()`.\n\n### Health Checking\n\nHealth checkers (`source/common/upstream/health_checker_impl.cc`) run periodic synthetic requests (HTTP GET to the health check path, TCP connect, gRPC health check). Results are tracked as `HealthFlag` bits on each `Host`:\n\n- `FAILED_ACTIVE_HC` \u2014 active health check has determined the host is unhealthy.\n- `FAILED_OUTLIER_CHECK` \u2014 outlier detection has ejected the host.\n- `FAILED_EDS_HEALTH` \u2014 xDS EDS marked the host unhealthy.\n\nOn a health check failure, the health checker calls `postThreadLocalHealthFailure(host)`, which posts to all worker threads to update the host's health flag and re-calculate the healthy host set. Because `LoadBalancer::chooseHost()` only draws from the healthy set, newly unhealthy hosts are excluded from selection within a single event loop cycle.\n\n### Outlier Detection\n\n`DetectorImpl` (`source/common/upstream/outlier_detection_impl.cc`) monitors per-host outcome data (5xx rate, consecutive 5xx, response latency via EWMA, success rate across the cluster). When a host's metrics cross a configured threshold, the detector:\n\n1. Sets `Host::HealthFlag::FAILED_OUTLIER_CHECK`.\n2. Calls the registered `addChangedStateCb` on `ClusterManagerImpl`, which posts `postThreadLocalHealthFailure(host)` to all workers.\n3. Schedules an ejection timer; after the ejection duration, the host is returned to the healthy set.\n\nThe router's `UpstreamRequest` reports upstream outcomes back to the outlier detector on stream completion, closing the feedback loop:\n\n```\nUpstreamRequest completion\n  -> Router::Filter::onUpstreamComplete()\n  -> host->outlierDetector().putHttpResponseCode(status_code)\n  -> DetectorImpl checks thresholds\n  -> eject host if threshold exceeded\n  -> postThreadLocalHealthFailure -> LB removes host from healthy set\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. End-to-End Data Flow\n\n### Request Path (Downstream to Upstream)\n\n```\n1. TCP bytes arrive on downstream connection\n   -> ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()\n   -> codec_->dispatch(data)            [H1/H2 codec parses bytes]\n\n2. Codec sees complete request headers\n   -> ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()  [creates ActiveStream]\n   -> ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()       [validates, traces, initializes timers]\n   -> FilterManager::decodeHeaders()      [iterates decoder filter chain A->B->...->Router]\n\n3. Each decoder filter processes headers\n   -> returns Continue / StopIteration / StopAllIterationAndBuffer\n\n4. Router filter (terminal decoder filter) receives headers\n   -> route_ = callbacks_->route()                 [RouteConfiguration match]\n   -> cluster = cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(name)    [TLS lookup, no lock]\n   -> host = cluster->chooseHost(this)             [LB selects endpoint]\n   -> generic_conn_pool = createConnPool(cluster, host)\n   -> UpstreamRequest created; acceptHeadersFromRouter() called\n\n5. UpstreamRequest feeds UpstreamFilterManager\n   -> Traverses upstream filter chain -> UpstreamCodecFilter\n   -> If connection ready: codec writes headers to upstream TCP connection\n   -> If not ready: UpstreamCodecFilter buffers; watermark back-pressure propagates\n\n6. Body and trailers follow same path via decodeData() / decodeTrailers()\n```\n\n### Response Path (Upstream to Downstream)\n\n```\n1. Upstream bytes arrive and are parsed by upstream codec\n   -> UpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders() / decodeData() / decodeTrailers()\n\n2. Response flows up through UpstreamFilterManager (upstream encoder direction)\n   -> UpstreamCodecFilter -> ... -> UpstreamRequest callbacks\n\n3. Router::Filter receives response\n   -> Checks retry_state_: retry or propagate?\n   -> On propagate: FilterManagerCallbacks::encodeHeaders() called\n\n4. FilterManager::encodeHeaders() iterates encoder_filters_ in REVERSE order\n   -> ...filter B -> filter A -> terminal (writes to ResponseEncoder)\n\n5. ActiveStream::encodeHeaders() writes to codec ResponseEncoder\n   -> H1/H2/H3 codec serializes headers to downstream TCP write buffer\n\n6. Connection-level watermarks propagate if write buffer fills:\n   -> onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark() -> codec -> per-stream flow control\n   -> Router suspends upstream reads; upstream TCP window closes\n```\n\n### Stream Teardown\n\nAfter the response is fully encoded:\n1. `ActiveStream::endStream()` is called, setting `codec_saw_local_complete_ = true`.\n2. `ConnectionManagerImpl::doEndStream()` checks whether the stream can be destroyed (`canDestroyStream()` \u2014 true when `codec_encode_complete_` or `on_reset_stream_called_` are set).\n3. `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` disarms all per-stream timers, calls `filter_manager_.onStreamComplete()` (which fires access logs), and schedules the `ActiveStream` for deferred deletion via `dispatcher_->deferredDelete()`.\n4. On H1, if the stream indicated drain-on-completion, `checkForDeferredClose()` transitions to `DrainState::Closing` and closes the connection.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points\n\nThe HCM is designed as an extension platform. The primary extension mechanisms are:\n\n### HTTP Filters\n\nThe most important extension point. Any code implementing `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, or `StreamFilter` and registered via the `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` extension registry can be inserted at any position in the `http_filters` list (except after the router, which must be terminal).\n\nNotable built-in extensions under `source/extensions/filters/http/`:\n- `ext_proc` \u2014 sends headers/body to an external gRPC server for transformation.\n- `wasm` \u2014 runs WebAssembly filters.\n- `lua` \u2014 inline Lua scripts.\n- `jwt_authn`, `oauth2`, `ext_authz` \u2014 authentication and authorization.\n- `grpc_json_transcoder` \u2014 translates REST to gRPC.\n- `buffer`, `local_ratelimit`, `ratelimit` \u2014 traffic shaping.\n- `compression` / `decompression` \u2014 gzip/brotli/zstd codecs.\n\n**Per-route filter configuration.** Each filter may expose `RouteSpecificFilterConfig` that overrides its behavior per virtual host or route. Filters access this via `StreamFilterCallbacks::mostSpecificPerFilterConfig()`.\n\n### Cluster Extensions\n\nCustom cluster types implement `ClusterFactory` and are registered under `envoy.cluster`. They control host discovery (e.g., EDS, STRICT_DNS, LOGICAL_DNS, custom Redis or aggregate clusters).\n\n### Load Balancer Extensions\n\nCustom load balancers implement `TypedLoadBalancerFactory`. The per-worker `LoadBalancer` is created by `TypedLoadBalancerFactory::create()`. Registered under `envoy.load_balancing_policies`.\n\n### Connection Pool / Upstream Transport Extensions\n\n`GenericConnPoolFactory` (registered under `envoy.upstreams`) controls how upstream connections are established. This is the hook for CONNECT tunneling, UDP proxying, or custom upstream protocols.\n\n### Access Loggers\n\nImplement `AccessLog::Instance` and register under `envoy.access_loggers`. Access loggers are called by `ActiveStream::log()` at stream start (periodically if configured), on stream completion, and optionally on upstream reset. Built-in loggers write to files, gRPC streams (ALS), or the OpenTelemetry logging API.\n\n### Health Check Extensions\n\nCustom health checkers implement `HealthCheckerFactory` (`envoy.health_checkers`). The `ClusterManagerImpl` wires the health checker to the cluster via `Cluster::healthChecker()`.\n\n### Request ID Extensions\n\nImplement `RequestIDExtension` to control how `x-request-id` is generated and propagated. The HCM calls `requestIDExtension()->setInRequest()` and `setInResponse()` at stream start and end.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Error Handling Summary\n\n| Stage | Error condition | Handling |\n|---|---|---|\n| Codec (H1/H2 parse) | Protocol violation, buffer flood | `handleCodecError()` \u2192 close connection with `FlushWriteAndDelay` |\n| Codec (overload) | `hcm_ondata_creating_codec_` sheds load | `handleCodecOverloadError()` \u2192 close connection |\n| Header validation (UHV) | Invalid request headers | `ActiveStream::validateHeaders()` sends 400; returns false to abort filter chain |\n| Decoder filter | Filter calls `sendLocalReply()` | Sets `decoder_filter_chain_aborted_`; runs encoder chain with synthetic response |\n| Decoder filter | Filter throws exception | Caught by Envoy's event loop; connection is closed |\n| Route selection | No matching route | Router sends 404 with `RouteNotFound` flag |\n| Cluster lookup | Cluster not found or maintenance | Router sends 503 with `NoClusterFound` / `UpstreamOverflow` |\n| Host selection | No healthy hosts | `sendNoHealthyUpstreamResponse()` \u2192 503 |\n| Connection pool | Connection failure | `onPoolFailure()` \u2192 `retry_state_->shouldRetry()` or 503 |\n| Upstream 5xx/reset | Bad upstream response | Router checks `retry_state_`; retries or sends upstream status downstream |\n| Per-try timeout | Attempt exceeds per-try deadline | `UpstreamRequest` reset; retry or 504 |\n| Global timeout | Stream exceeds max duration | `onStreamMaxDurationReached()` \u2192 504 |\n| Outlier detection | Host exceeds error thresholds | Host ejected from healthy set; future `chooseHost()` calls avoid it |\n| Downstream disconnect | Remote or local close during stream | `resetAllStreams()` with `ConnectionTermination`; access logs still fire |\n| Zombie streams | Codec encode complete but response encoder still exists | Stream tracked as zombie; `doEndStream()` deferred until codec signals completion |\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"
}

{
  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager: Architecture Document\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP traffic. It is implemented as a `Network::ReadFilter` \u2014 a plugin in Envoy's L4 filter chain \u2014 that takes ownership of a downstream TCP (or QUIC) connection and converts the raw byte stream into a sequence of HTTP request/response lifecycle events. Four primary components collaborate to move a request from arrival on the wire to dispatch upstream and back:\n\n1. **`ConnectionManagerImpl`** \u2014 owns the connection and its codec; creates `ActiveStream` objects per request.\n2. **`FilterManager` / `DownstreamFilterManager`** \u2014 owns the per-stream HTTP filter chain and drives it forward.\n3. **Router `Filter`** \u2014 the terminal decoder filter; selects a cluster, obtains a connection pool, and forwards the request.\n4. **`ClusterManagerImpl`** \u2014 manages cluster topology, load balancing, and connection pools.\n\nThe source code lives primarily under:\n\n| Component | Source files |\n|---|---|\n| ConnectionManagerImpl | `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.{h,cc}` |\n| FilterManager | `source/common/http/filter_manager.{h,cc}` |\n| Router Filter | `source/common/router/router.{h,cc}`, `source/common/router/upstream_request.{h,cc}` |\n| ClusterManager | `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.{h,cc}` |\n| HTTP/1 codec | `source/common/http/http1/` |\n| HTTP/2 codec | `source/common/http/http2/` |\n| Connection pools | `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.{h,cc}`, `source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.*`, `source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.*`, `source/common/http/conn_pool_grid.*` |\n| Outlier detection | `source/common/upstream/outlier_detection_impl.{h,cc}` |\n| Health checking | `source/common/upstream/health_checker_impl.{h,cc}` |\n\n---\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl` (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h`) is the network-layer entry point for HTTP traffic. It implements three interfaces simultaneously:\n\n- **`Network::ReadFilter`** \u2014 receives raw bytes arriving on the downstream TCP connection.\n- **`Http::ServerConnectionCallbacks`** \u2014 receives per-stream notifications from the HTTP codec (new stream, GoAway).\n- **`Network::ConnectionCallbacks`** \u2014 receives connection-level events (close, watermark changes).\n\nIt is instantiated once per downstream connection by the HCM extension factory (`source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc`) and wired into Envoy's L4 filter chain at connection acceptance time.\n\n### Codec Creation (Lazy Instantiation)\n\nFor HTTP/1.x and HTTP/2, `ConnectionManagerImpl` does not create a codec until the first `onData()` call arrives:\n\n```\n// source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc, onData()\nif (!codec_) {\n    createCodec(data);\n}\nconst Status status = codec_->dispatch(data);\n```\n\n`createCodec()` delegates to `ConnectionManagerConfig::createCodec()`, which inspects the first bytes of `data` to distinguish HTTP/1 from HTTP/2 (the H2 client preface `PRI * HTTP/2.0\\r\\n\\r\\nSM\\r\\n\\r\\n`). The resulting `ServerConnection` (H1 or H2 implementation) is stored in `codec_`.\n\nFor HTTP/3 (QUIC), the protocol is known at connection time, so the codec is created eagerly in `onNewConnection()` before any `onData()` arrives:\n\n```\n// source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc, onNewConnection()\ncreateCodec(dummy);\nASSERT(codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http3);\nreturn Network::FilterStatus::StopIteration; // QUIC bypasses onData entirely\n```\n\nThis means H3 connections stop L4 filter iteration immediately; QUICHE handles stream demultiplexing internally and delivers decoded events directly to the codec callbacks.\n\n### ActiveStream Creation\n\nWhen the codec parses a complete set of request headers from the wire, it calls back `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()`. This function:\n\n1. Allocates a `Buffer::BufferMemoryAccount` for watermark tracking, wired to the downstream `ResponseEncoder`.\n2. Constructs an `ActiveStream` object, giving it a back-reference to the `ConnectionManagerImpl` and a `DownstreamFilterManager`.\n3. Prepends the new stream to the `streams_` linked list and returns it as the `RequestDecoder` for the codec to use for subsequent `decodeHeaders` / `decodeData` / `decodeTrailers` calls.\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\nauto new_stream = std::make_unique<ActiveStream>(\n    *this, response_encoder.getStream().bufferLimit(), std::move(downstream_stream_account));\nLinkedList::moveIntoList(std::move(new_stream), streams_);\nreturn **streams_.begin();\n```\n\n`ActiveStream` is a heavyweight struct that aggregates the `DownstreamFilterManager`, cached route, request/response header maps, timers, and tracing span for a single HTTP exchange. It implements `RequestDecoder` so the codec can push bytes into it, and `FilterManagerCallbacks` so the filter chain can push encoded responses back toward the codec.\n\n### Connection-Level Concerns\n\n**Drain decisions.** `ConnectionManagerImpl` holds a reference to `Network::DrainDecision`. On each new stream, it checks `maxRequestsPerConnection`; when that limit is reached on H2/H3, it calls `startDrainSequence()` which sends a GOAWAY frame and transitions to `DrainState::Draining`. When the stream count reaches zero, `checkForDeferredClose()` closes the TCP connection.\n\n**Overload management.** Two `Server::LoadShedPoint` handles are acquired at construction from `OverloadManager`:\n- `HcmDecodeHeaders` \u2014 checked at `decodeHeaders` time; sheds load by sending 503 and stopping iteration.\n- `HcmCodecCreation` \u2014 checked in `onData()` before codec instantiation; closes the connection before any work is done.\n\nAdditionally, two `OverloadActionState` references \u2014 `overload_stop_accepting_requests_ref_` and `overload_disable_keepalive_ref_` \u2014 are cached at construction and checked in the hot path without requiring a map lookup.\n\n**Watermark-based flow control.** The `ConnectionManagerImpl` implements `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` and `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`, which delegate directly into the codec:\n\n```cpp\nvoid onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark() override {\n    codec_->onUnderlyingConnectionAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark();\n}\n```\n\nThe H2 codec propagates these signals to per-stream flow control windows; the H1 codec pauses reads on the connection. Individual `ActiveStream` objects also track watermark state and propagate it to the decoder filter chain via `FilterManager::onDecoderFilterAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()`.\n\n**Request deferral across I/O cycles.** The runtime key `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` limits how many requests can be fully processed in a single read event. Additional requests are deferred to a schedulable callback (`deferred_request_processing_callback_`). This prevents a single connection from monopolizing the event loop under H2 or H3 multiplexing.\n\n**Timers per connection.** `initializeReadFilterCallbacks()` arms:\n- `connection_idle_timer_` \u2014 fires `onIdleTimeout()` if no streams are active for the configured duration.\n- `connection_duration_timer_` \u2014 fires `onConnectionDurationTimeout()` after the maximum connection age.\n\nThese are _connection-level_ timers that coexist with the _per-stream_ timers managed inside `ActiveStream`.\n\n### Error Handling\n\nCodec errors (protocol violations, buffer flood attacks, inbound frames with empty payloads, overload errors) are caught at the `codec_->dispatch(data)` call site. `handleCodecError()` and `handleCodecOverloadError()` record the appropriate response flag, then call `doConnectionClose()` with `FlushWriteAndDelay`, which:\n1. Resets all active streams with `StreamResetReason::ConnectionTermination`.\n2. Calls `connection().close()` on the underlying network connection.\n\n---\n\n## 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain\n\n### Class Hierarchy\n\n`FilterManager` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.h`) is the abstract base; `DownstreamFilterManager` is the concrete subclass used for downstream (client-to-proxy) streams. A separate `UpstreamFilterManager` is used for the upstream side inside `UpstreamRequest`. `FilterManager` owns two parallel vectors:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/filter_manager.h\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n    std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n    // Iterates forward: A -> B -> C\n};\n\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n    std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n    // Iterates in reverse: C -> B -> A\n};\n```\n\nEach entry wraps a user-provided filter handle (`StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, or `StreamFilter` for dual-purpose) and tracks per-filter iteration state.\n\n### Filter Chain Construction\n\n`FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` is called once per stream during `ActiveStream` initialization, before the first `decodeHeaders` call. The HCM configuration object (`source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc`) implements `FilterChainFactory`. It iterates over the ordered list of `HttpFilterFactory` functions configured via `http_filters`, calling:\n\n```cpp\ncallbacks.addStreamDecoderFilter(filter);\ncallbacks.addStreamEncoderFilter(filter);\n// or, for dual-purpose filters:\ncallbacks.addStreamFilter(filter);\n```\n\nThese append `ActiveStreamDecoderFilter` or `ActiveStreamEncoderFilter` wrappers to the respective vectors. The router filter (the terminal filter) is always last in the decoder chain; the `UpstreamCodecFilter` is always last in the upstream filter chain.\n\n### Decoder Filter Iteration (Request Path)\n\nWhen `ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()` is called by the codec, it validates the header map (if UHV is enabled) and then calls `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()`. This function iterates `decoder_filters_` from beginning to end, calling each filter's `decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` method:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/filter_manager.cc\nfor (; entry != decoder_filters_.end(); entry++) {\n    FilterHeadersStatus status = (*entry)->handle_->decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream);\n    const auto continue_iteration =\n        (*entry)->commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback(status, end_stream);\n    if (!continue_iteration && std::next(entry) != decoder_filters_.end()) {\n        maybeContinueDecoding(continue_data_entry);\n        return; // pause here\n    }\n}\n```\n\nA filter controls iteration by its return value:\n\n| Return value | Effect |\n|---|---|\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::Continue` | Proceed to the next filter immediately. |\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::StopIteration` | Pause iteration; filter must later call `continueDecoding()`. |\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::StopAllIterationAndBuffer` | Pause and buffer all subsequent data until resumed. |\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::StopAllIterationAndWatermark` | Pause and apply watermark-based back pressure. |\n| `FilterHeadersStatus::ContinueAndDontEndStream` | Continue but strip the end-stream flag (allows injecting a body). |\n\n`decodeData()` and `decodeTrailers()` follow the same pattern. Each call records a `latest_data_decoding_filter_` pointer so that subsequent data injected by a filter is only forwarded to filters _after_ the injecting filter, preventing double-processing.\n\n### Resuming Iteration\n\n`ActiveStreamDecoderFilter::continueDecoding()` calls `commonContinue()` on the base class. This:\n1. Sets `iteration_state_` back to `Continue`.\n2. If the filter had stopped with `StopAll`, sets `iterate_from_current_filter_ = true` so iteration restarts from the paused filter rather than the next one.\n3. Resumes `do1xxHeaders()`, `doHeaders()`, `doData()`, and `doTrailers()` in order.\n\n### Encoder Filter Iteration (Response Path)\n\nWhen the router filter receives a response from upstream, it calls back into the `FilterManager` via `FilterManagerCallbacks::encodeHeaders()`. The `FilterManager` iterates `encoder_filters_` in **reverse** order (last-configured to first-configured), ensuring symmetric wrapping: a filter that transforms the request also wraps the response.\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/filter_manager.h\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n    using Iterator = std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr>::reverse_iterator;\n    Iterator begin() { return entries_.rbegin(); }\n    Iterator end()   { return entries_.rend(); }\n};\n```\n\n### Local Replies\n\nAny filter may call `sendLocalReply(code, body, modify_headers, grpc_status, details)` to terminate the request without forwarding it upstream. This:\n1. Sets a `LocalReplyOwnerObject` in filter state identifying the originating filter.\n2. Delegates to `FilterManager::sendLocalReply()`, which synthesizes a response header map and runs it through the encoder filter chain.\n3. Sets `decoder_filter_chain_aborted_ = true`, causing all subsequent decoder filter calls to short-circuit.\n\n### Filter Type Taxonomy\n\n| Interface | Direction | When used |\n|---|---|---|\n| `StreamDecoderFilter` | Request only | Auth filters, body inspection, header manipulation |\n| `StreamEncoderFilter` | Response only | Response compression, header stripping |\n| `StreamFilter` | Both | External processing (ext_proc), WASM, Lua filters |\n\nAll three share `StreamFilterBase::onDestroy()` for cleanup when the stream ends.\n\n### Access Logging\n\n`FilterManager` accumulates access log handlers from two sources: the HCM-level `accessLogs()` list from `ConnectionManagerConfig`, and per-filter handlers added via `FilterManagerCallbacks::accessLogHandlers()`. These are merged in `ActiveStream::accessLogHandlers()` and fired on stream completion.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Router Filter\n\n### Role in the Pipeline\n\nThe router filter (`source/common/router/router.h`, class `Filter`) is always the last filter in the decoder chain. It implements `Http::StreamDecoderFilter` and `Upstream::LoadBalancerContextBase`. Unlike most filters that transform traffic and pass it along, the router filter consumes the request and originates a new one upstream via `UpstreamRequest`.\n\n### Route Selection\n\nIn `Filter::decodeHeaders()`, after validation of strict check headers, route selection proceeds:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/router/router.cc\nroute_ = callbacks_->route();\n```\n\n`callbacks_->route()` calls into `ActiveStream::route()`, which consults the snapped `RouteConfiguration` (an `ActiveStream`-local snapshot of the RDS configuration taken when the stream begins). The route configuration (`source/common/router/config_impl.cc`) evaluates each `VirtualHost` and its `Route` entries in configuration order, matching on `:authority`, path prefix/regex/exact, headers, and query parameters. The first match wins.\n\nIf no route matches, the router sends a 404 via `sendLocalReply()` and returns `StopIteration`.\n\nIf the matched route has a `direct_response`, the router synthesizes the configured response locally and never contacts upstream.\n\nIf the matched route has a `route_entry`, the router extracts `route_entry_->clusterName()` and looks up the cluster:\n\n```cpp\nUpstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster =\n    config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName());\n```\n\nThis lookup is thread-local and lock-free (see \u00a74). If the cluster does not exist, a 503 with `NoClusterFound` response flag is returned.\n\n### Host Selection and Connection Pool Acquisition\n\nAfter cluster lookup, the router calls `cluster->chooseHost(this)` where `this` implements `LoadBalancerContext`. This interface provides:\n- `computeHashKey()` \u2014 for consistent-hash load balancers, derived from header-based hash policy configured on the route or cluster.\n- `metadataMatchCriteria()` \u2014 for metadata-based subset routing.\n- `downstreamConnection()` \u2014 allows the LB to read downstream SSL/connection attributes.\n\nHost selection may be synchronous (common case) or asynchronous (e.g., when waiting for an on-demand cluster). In the synchronous path, `continueDecodeHeaders()` is called immediately. In the asynchronous path, the filter returns `StopAllIterationAndWatermark` and stores a callback to resume when the host is ready.\n\nOnce a host is selected, `createConnPool()` obtains a `GenericConnPool` from the cluster's factory:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/router/router.cc\nstd::unique_ptr<GenericConnPool> generic_conn_pool = createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host);\n```\n\nThe `GenericConnPool` wraps an HTTP or TCP connection pool selected based on the route's `upstream_protocol` (HTTP, TCP for CONNECT tunneling, or UDP for CONNECT-UDP).\n\n### UpstreamRequest Lifecycle\n\n`UpstreamRequest` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.h`) encapsulates a single attempt to forward the request to a specific upstream host. The router may hold multiple `UpstreamRequest` objects simultaneously (one primary + hedged retries).\n\n```cpp\nUpstreamRequestPtr upstream_request = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(\n    *this, std::move(generic_conn_pool), can_send_early_data,\n    can_use_http3, enable_half_close);\nLinkedList::moveIntoList(std::move(upstream_request), upstream_requests_);\nupstream_requests_.front()->acceptHeadersFromRouter(end_stream);\n```\n\nInternally, `UpstreamRequest` owns an `UpstreamFilterManager` (a second, upstream-side filter chain). Headers and body flow through this chain until they reach the terminal `UpstreamCodecFilter`, which writes them to the upstream HTTP codec. If the upstream connection is not yet ready, `UpstreamCodecFilter` returns `StopAllIteration`, causing the `UpstreamFilterManager` to buffer data and apply watermarks back toward the router.\n\nWhen the upstream connection pool signals success via `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks::onPoolReady()`, the `UpstreamCodecFilter` flushes buffered data and begins streaming.\n\nResponse data arriving from upstream travels the reverse path: the upstream codec delivers frames to `UpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders()` / `decodeData()` / `decodeTrailers()`, which feed back through the `UpstreamFilterManager` and then call `RouterFilterInterface` callbacks on the `Filter`, which in turn calls `FilterManagerCallbacks::encodeHeaders()` to begin the downstream encoder filter chain.\n\n### Retry Logic\n\n`retry_state_` is created in `continueDecodeHeaders()` from the route's `RetryPolicy`:\n\n```cpp\nretry_state_ = createRetryState(*getEffectiveRetryPolicy(), headers, *cluster_,\n                                 request_vcluster_, route_stats_context_,\n                                 config_->factory_context_, callbacks_->dispatcher(),\n                                 route_entry_->priority());\n```\n\n`RetryStateImpl` (`source/common/router/retry_state_impl.cc`) tracks the number of attempts, retry-on conditions (5xx, reset, connect-failure, retriable status codes), and the current backoff interval. When an `UpstreamRequest` fails (connection error, 5xx response, per-try timeout), the router calls `retry_state_->shouldRetry()`. If retrying, a new `UpstreamRequest` is constructed and prepended to `upstream_requests_`, and the failed one is reset and removed.\n\n### Timeout Handling\n\n`FilterUtility::finalTimeout()` computes two timeouts:\n\n- **Global timeout** \u2014 enforced by a timer on `ActiveStream` (`max_stream_duration_timer_`). When it fires, the router sends a 504 locally.\n- **Per-try timeout** \u2014 set up via `UpstreamRequest::setupPerTryTimeout()`. When it fires, the current attempt is reset and retried (if `hedge_on_per_try_timeout` is configured, a new attempt is started _before_ the old one is cancelled, enabling hedging).\n\n### Shadow Routing\n\nIn `continueDecodeHeaders()`, after the primary `UpstreamRequest` is created, the router evaluates shadow policies from the route or cluster configuration. For each active shadow:\n\n```cpp\nHttp::AsyncClient::OngoingRequest* shadow_stream =\n    config_->shadowWriter().streamingShadow(cluster_name, shadow_headers, options);\n```\n\n`ShadowWriterImpl` (`source/common/router/shadow_writer_impl.cc`) sends the mirrored request via the HTTP async client. Shadow responses are discarded. Shadow streams are tracked in `shadow_streams_` and cancelled on stream destruction.\n\n### Error Handling\n\n| Failure | Router action |\n|---|---|\n| No route | `sendLocalReply(404, RouteNotFound)` |\n| Cluster not found | `sendLocalReply(503, ClusterNotFound)` |\n| No healthy upstream | `sendLocalReply(503, NoHealthyUpstream)` |\n| Maintenance mode | `sendLocalReply(503, MaintenanceMode)` |\n| Connection pool failure | Reset `UpstreamRequest`; check `retry_state_` |\n| Upstream 5xx / reset | Consult `retry_state_`; retry or propagate 5xx downstream |\n| Global timeout | `sendLocalReply(504, ResponseTimeout)` |\n| Per-try timeout (hedging off) | Reset attempt; retry if budget allows |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n### ClusterManagerImpl Architecture\n\n`ClusterManagerImpl` (`source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h`) is a singleton that maintains all cluster state in a thread-safe manner. Because Envoy uses a single-threaded event loop per worker thread, the cluster manager uses a thread-local storage pattern:\n\n- **Main thread** holds authoritative `ClusterData` objects (the `active_clusters_` and `warming_clusters_` maps).\n- **Each worker thread** holds a `ThreadLocalClusterManagerImpl` with its own `thread_local_clusters_` map, each containing per-host connection pools.\n\nCluster updates (from xDS/CDS) are applied on the main thread and then posted to all worker threads via `tls_.runOnAllThreads()`. This means each worker thread sees a consistent snapshot of cluster state without locks.\n\nThe `getThreadLocalCluster(name)` method (called by the router on the hot path) performs a simple hash map lookup against `thread_local_clusters_` \u2014 no locking, no cross-thread communication.\n\n### Load Balancing\n\nEach `ThreadLocalClusterManagerImpl::ClusterEntry` owns a `LoadBalancer` instance specific to that worker thread. When the router calls `cluster->chooseHost(context)`, it delegates to `lb_->chooseHost(context)`. Envoy ships several built-in load balancer implementations:\n\n- **Round robin** (`source/common/upstream/round_robin_lb.cc`) \u2014 cycles through the healthy host set.\n- **Least request** (`source/common/upstream/least_request_lb.cc`) \u2014 picks the host with fewest active requests using O(2) power-of-two-choices sampling.\n- **Random** (`source/common/upstream/random_lb.cc`) \u2014 uniform random selection.\n- **Ring hash / Maglev** (`source/common/upstream/ring_hash_lb.cc`, `maglev_lb.cc`) \u2014 consistent hashing; uses `LoadBalancerContext::computeHashKey()`.\n- **Subset LB** (`source/common/upstream/subset_lb.cc`) \u2014 wraps another LB; selects hosts matching `MetadataMatchCriteria`.\n\nAll built-in LBs operate on the **priority set** \u2014 an ordered collection of `HostSet` objects, one per priority level. Hosts that fail health checks or outlier detection are removed from the healthy set and are not selected.\n\n### Connection Pool Mechanics\n\n`ClusterEntry::httpConnPool()` (in `cluster_manager_impl.cc`) returns an `HttpPoolData` wrapping an `Http::ConnectionPool::Instance`:\n\n```cpp\nabsl::optional<HttpPoolData>\nClusterEntry::httpConnPool(HostConstSharedPtr host, ResourcePriority priority,\n                           absl::optional<Http::Protocol> protocol,\n                           LoadBalancerContext* context) {\n    auto pool = httpConnPoolImpl(host, priority, protocol, context);\n    ...\n    HttpPoolData data([this, priority, protocol, context]() {\n        maybePreconnect(...); // preconnect on each new stream\n    }, pool);\n    return data;\n}\n```\n\nEach pool is keyed by `(host, priority, protocol)`. Pools are created lazily on first use and are stored in `PriorityConnPoolMap<Http::ConnectionPool::Instance>`.\n\nThe concrete pool classes are:\n- `Http1ConnPoolImpl` (`source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.cc`) \u2014 one request per TCP connection; connections are not reused until the response is complete.\n- `Http2ConnPoolImpl` (`source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.cc`) \u2014 multiplexes many streams over one TCP connection; governed by `max_concurrent_streams`.\n- `ConnPoolGrid` (`source/common/http/conn_pool_grid.cc`) \u2014 tries HTTP/3 first (if QUIC is available), with automatic fallback to HTTP/2 or HTTP/1. Uses `HttpServerPropertiesCache` to remember per-origin protocol capabilities.\n\nThe shared base `HttpConnPoolImplBase` (`source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h`) implements stream queuing via `HttpPendingStream` objects. When `newStream()` is called:\n1. If a ready connection exists with capacity, the stream is attached immediately via `onPoolReady()`.\n2. Otherwise, a `HttpPendingStream` is enqueued. When a connection becomes available (either an existing one frees capacity, or a new one finishes the TLS handshake), the pending stream is dequeued and attached.\n\n**Preconnect.** After each new stream is established, `maybePreconnect()` is called speculatively to open an additional connection if the predicted load warrants it. The decision is based on `peekahead_ratio` and current `pending_streams_ / connecting_and_connected_stream_capacity_` ratios, mirroring the logic in `ConnPoolImplBase::shouldConnect()`.\n\n### Health Checking\n\nHealth checkers (`source/common/upstream/health_checker_impl.cc`) run periodic synthetic requests (HTTP GET to the health check path, TCP connect, gRPC health check). Results are tracked as `HealthFlag` bits on each `Host`:\n\n- `FAILED_ACTIVE_HC` \u2014 active health check has determined the host is unhealthy.\n- `FAILED_OUTLIER_CHECK` \u2014 outlier detection has ejected the host.\n- `FAILED_EDS_HEALTH` \u2014 xDS EDS marked the host unhealthy.\n\nOn a health check failure, the health checker calls `postThreadLocalHealthFailure(host)`, which posts to all worker threads to update the host's health flag and re-calculate the healthy host set. Because `LoadBalancer::chooseHost()` only draws from the healthy set, newly unhealthy hosts are excluded from selection within a single event loop cycle.\n\n### Outlier Detection\n\n`DetectorImpl` (`source/common/upstream/outlier_detection_impl.cc`) monitors per-host outcome data (5xx rate, consecutive 5xx, response latency via EWMA, success rate across the cluster). When a host's metrics cross a configured threshold, the detector:\n\n1. Sets `Host::HealthFlag::FAILED_OUTLIER_CHECK`.\n2. Calls the registered `addChangedStateCb` on `ClusterManagerImpl`, which posts `postThreadLocalHealthFailure(host)` to all workers.\n3. Schedules an ejection timer; after the ejection duration, the host is returned to the healthy set.\n\nThe router's `UpstreamRequest` reports upstream outcomes back to the outlier detector on stream completion, closing the feedback loop:\n\n```\nUpstreamRequest completion\n  -> Router::Filter::onUpstreamComplete()\n  -> host->outlierDetector().putHttpResponseCode(status_code)\n  -> DetectorImpl checks thresholds\n  -> eject host if threshold exceeded\n  -> postThreadLocalHealthFailure -> LB removes host from healthy set\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. End-to-End Data Flow\n\n### Request Path (Downstream to Upstream)\n\n```\n1. TCP bytes arrive on downstream connection\n   -> ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()\n   -> codec_->dispatch(data)            [H1/H2 codec parses bytes]\n\n2. Codec sees complete request headers\n   -> ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()  [creates ActiveStream]\n   -> ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()       [validates, traces, initializes timers]\n   -> FilterManager::decodeHeaders()      [iterates decoder filter chain A->B->...->Router]\n\n3. Each decoder filter processes headers\n   -> returns Continue / StopIteration / StopAllIterationAndBuffer\n\n4. Router filter (terminal decoder filter) receives headers\n   -> route_ = callbacks_->route()                 [RouteConfiguration match]\n   -> cluster = cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(name)    [TLS lookup, no lock]\n   -> host = cluster->chooseHost(this)             [LB selects endpoint]\n   -> generic_conn_pool = createConnPool(cluster, host)\n   -> UpstreamRequest created; acceptHeadersFromRouter() called\n\n5. UpstreamRequest feeds UpstreamFilterManager\n   -> Traverses upstream filter chain -> UpstreamCodecFilter\n   -> If connection ready: codec writes headers to upstream TCP connection\n   -> If not ready: UpstreamCodecFilter buffers; watermark back-pressure propagates\n\n6. Body and trailers follow same path via decodeData() / decodeTrailers()\n```\n\n### Response Path (Upstream to Downstream)\n\n```\n1. Upstream bytes arrive and are parsed by upstream codec\n   -> UpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders() / decodeData() / decodeTrailers()\n\n2. Response flows up through UpstreamFilterManager (upstream encoder direction)\n   -> UpstreamCodecFilter -> ... -> UpstreamRequest callbacks\n\n3. Router::Filter receives response\n   -> Checks retry_state_: retry or propagate?\n   -> On propagate: FilterManagerCallbacks::encodeHeaders() called\n\n4. FilterManager::encodeHeaders() iterates encoder_filters_ in REVERSE order\n   -> ...filter B -> filter A -> terminal (writes to ResponseEncoder)\n\n5. ActiveStream::encodeHeaders() writes to codec ResponseEncoder\n   -> H1/H2/H3 codec serializes headers to downstream TCP write buffer\n\n6. Connection-level watermarks propagate if write buffer fills:\n   -> onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark() -> codec -> per-stream flow control\n   -> Router suspends upstream reads; upstream TCP window closes\n```\n\n### Stream Teardown\n\nAfter the response is fully encoded:\n1. `ActiveStream::endStream()` is called, setting `codec_saw_local_complete_ = true`.\n2. `ConnectionManagerImpl::doEndStream()` checks whether the stream can be destroyed (`canDestroyStream()` \u2014 true when `codec_encode_complete_` or `on_reset_stream_called_` are set).\n3. `doDeferredStreamDestroy()` disarms all per-stream timers, calls `filter_manager_.onStreamComplete()` (which fires access logs), and schedules the `ActiveStream` for deferred deletion via `dispatcher_->deferredDelete()`.\n4. On H1, if the stream indicated drain-on-completion, `checkForDeferredClose()` transitions to `DrainState::Closing` and closes the connection.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points\n\nThe HCM is designed as an extension platform. The primary extension mechanisms are:\n\n### HTTP Filters\n\nThe most important extension point. Any code implementing `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, or `StreamFilter` and registered via the `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` extension registry can be inserted at any position in the `http_filters` list (except after the router, which must be terminal).\n\nNotable built-in extensions under `source/extensions/filters/http/`:\n- `ext_proc` \u2014 sends headers/body to an external gRPC server for transformation.\n- `wasm` \u2014 runs WebAssembly filters.\n- `lua` \u2014 inline Lua scripts.\n- `jwt_authn`, `oauth2`, `ext_authz` \u2014 authentication and authorization.\n- `grpc_json_transcoder` \u2014 translates REST to gRPC.\n- `buffer`, `local_ratelimit`, `ratelimit` \u2014 traffic shaping.\n- `compression` / `decompression` \u2014 gzip/brotli/zstd codecs.\n\n**Per-route filter configuration.** Each filter may expose `RouteSpecificFilterConfig` that overrides its behavior per virtual host or route. Filters access this via `StreamFilterCallbacks::mostSpecificPerFilterConfig()`.\n\n### Cluster Extensions\n\nCustom cluster types implement `ClusterFactory` and are registered under `envoy.cluster`. They control host discovery (e.g., EDS, STRICT_DNS, LOGICAL_DNS, custom Redis or aggregate clusters).\n\n### Load Balancer Extensions\n\nCustom load balancers implement `TypedLoadBalancerFactory`. The per-worker `LoadBalancer` is created by `TypedLoadBalancerFactory::create()`. Registered under `envoy.load_balancing_policies`.\n\n### Connection Pool / Upstream Transport Extensions\n\n`GenericConnPoolFactory` (registered under `envoy.upstreams`) controls how upstream connections are established. This is the hook for CONNECT tunneling, UDP proxying, or custom upstream protocols.\n\n### Access Loggers\n\nImplement `AccessLog::Instance` and register under `envoy.access_loggers`. Access loggers are called by `ActiveStream::log()` at stream start (periodically if configured), on stream completion, and optionally on upstream reset. Built-in loggers write to files, gRPC streams (ALS), or the OpenTelemetry logging API.\n\n### Health Check Extensions\n\nCustom health checkers implement `HealthCheckerFactory` (`envoy.health_checkers`). The `ClusterManagerImpl` wires the health checker to the cluster via `Cluster::healthChecker()`.\n\n### Request ID Extensions\n\nImplement `RequestIDExtension` to control how `x-request-id` is generated and propagated. The HCM calls `requestIDExtension()->setInRequest()` and `setInResponse()` at stream start and end.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Error Handling Summary\n\n| Stage | Error condition | Handling |\n|---|---|---|\n| Codec (H1/H2 parse) | Protocol violation, buffer flood | `handleCodecError()` \u2192 close connection with `FlushWriteAndDelay` |\n| Codec (overload) | `hcm_ondata_creating_codec_` sheds load | `handleCodecOverloadError()` \u2192 close connection |\n| Header validation (UHV) | Invalid request headers | `ActiveStream::validateHeaders()` sends 400; returns false to abort filter chain |\n| Decoder filter | Filter calls `sendLocalReply()` | Sets `decoder_filter_chain_aborted_`; runs encoder chain with synthetic response |\n| Decoder filter | Filter throws exception | Caught by Envoy's event loop; connection is closed |\n| Route selection | No matching route | Router sends 404 with `RouteNotFound` flag |\n| Cluster lookup | Cluster not found or maintenance | Router sends 503 with `NoClusterFound` / `UpstreamOverflow` |\n| Host selection | No healthy hosts | `sendNoHealthyUpstreamResponse()` \u2192 503 |\n| Connection pool | Connection failure | `onPoolFailure()` \u2192 `retry_state_->shouldRetry()` or 503 |\n| Upstream 5xx/reset | Bad upstream response | Router checks `retry_state_`; retries or sends upstream status downstream |\n| Per-try timeout | Attempt exceeds per-try deadline | `UpstreamRequest` reset; retry or 504 |\n| Global timeout | Stream exceeds max duration | `onStreamMaxDurationReached()` \u2192 504 |\n| Outlier detection | Host exceeds error thresholds | Host ejected from healthy set; future `chooseHost()` calls avoid it |\n| Downstream disconnect | Remote or local close during stream | `resetAllStreams()` with `ConnectionTermination`; access logs still fire |\n| Zombie streams | Codec encode complete but response encoder still exists | Stream tracked as zombie; `doEndStream()` deferred until codec signals completion |\n",

# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager: Architecture Document

## Overview

The HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP traffic. It is implemented as a `Network::ReadFilter` — a plugin in Envoy's L4 filter chain — that takes ownership of a downstream TCP (or QUIC) connection and converts the raw byte stream into a sequence of HTTP request/response lifecycle events. Four primary components collaborate to move a request from arrival on the wire to dispatch upstream and back:

1. **`ConnectionManagerImpl`** — owns the connection and its codec; creates `ActiveStream` objects per request.
2. **`FilterManager` / `DownstreamFilterManager`** — owns the per-stream HTTP filter chain and drives it forward.
3. **Router `Filter`** — the terminal decoder filter; selects a cluster, obtains a connection pool, and forwards the request.
4. **`ClusterManagerImpl`** — manages cluster topology, load balancing, and connection pools.

The source code lives primarily under:

| Component | Source files |
|---|---|
| ConnectionManagerImpl | `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.{h,cc}` |
| FilterManager | `source/common/http/filter_manager.{h,cc}` |
| Router Filter | `source/common/router/router.{h,cc}`, `source/common/router/upstream_request.{h,cc}` |
| ClusterManager | `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.{h,cc}` |
| HTTP/1 codec | `source/common/http/http1/` |
| HTTP/2 codec | `source/common/http/http2/` |
| Connection pools | `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.{h,cc}`, `source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.*`, `source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.*`, `source/common/http/conn_pool_grid.*` |
| Outlier detection | `source/common/upstream/outlier_detection_impl.{h,cc}` |
| Health checking | `source/common/upstream/health_checker_impl.{h,cc}` |
